<div id="review_2738674546" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2738674546" />
    <a title="Matthew Quann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22699228-matthew-quann"><img alt="Matthew Quann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528393487p2/22699228.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2738674546?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew Quann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew Quann" href="/user/show/22699228-matthew-quann">Matthew Quann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781407189147" href="/book/show/40493462-mortal-engines">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22699228-matthew-quann?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22699228-matthew-quann?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2738674546" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16197383701903268229">YA fantasy and sci-fi aren't my usual cup of tea, but I ended up having a good bit of fun with Philip Reeve's early-2000's hit. The story moves quickly and manages to pack in some interesting world-building. I've done my best to avoid most post-apocalyptic stuff of late, but this far-distant future where mechanized cities roam the land was original and well realized. I was also impressed with the subversion of the "beautiful young people fall in love" trope, and I'm sad to see that the Hollywood</span>
  <span id="freeText16197383701903268229" style="display:none">YA fantasy and sci-fi aren't my usual cup of tea, but I ended up having a good bit of fun with Philip Reeve's early-2000's hit. The story moves quickly and manages to pack in some interesting world-building. I've done my best to avoid most post-apocalyptic stuff of late, but this far-distant future where mechanized cities roam the land was original and well realized. I was also impressed with the subversion of the "beautiful young people fall in love" trope, and I'm sad to see that the Hollywood adaptation decided to forgo depicting Hester's scar.<br /><br />My complaints, if any, are really petty since the book is clearly aimed at a younger audience. The plot is quite predictable, the characters recap and ruminate regularly, and there's little subtlety in the menacing villains. With that said, I would have loved this book as a young teen, and still managed to get a pretty good kick out of it as an adult. Overall, an enjoyable YA romp!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16197383701903268229" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_769838912" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/769838912" />
    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1143969-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1409947508p2/1143969.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/769838912?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/1143969-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12279235-mortal-engines">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=othercities">othercities</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=great-villains">great-villains</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=rereads">rereads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=favourite">favourite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=futuristic">futuristic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=endcoming">endcoming</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer769838912" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12529355498693748543"><blockquote>It was a dark, blustery afternoon in spring, and the city of London was chasing a small mining town across the dried-out bed of the old North Sea.</blockquote><br/>Man, I love that opening line: it immediately raises so many questions, and weirdly reminds me of Stephen King's inimitable <i>The man in black fled across the desert, and the gunslinger followed.</i> It immediately plunges you into a chase scene with an urge to know more and see what happens.<br/><br/>I needed something light and whimsical after my previous book, so t</span>
  <span id="freeText12529355498693748543" style="display:none"><blockquote>It was a dark, blustery afternoon in spring, and the city of London was chasing a small mining town across the dried-out bed of the old North Sea.</blockquote><br />Man, I love that opening line: it immediately raises so many questions, and weirdly reminds me of Stephen King's inimitable <i>The man in black fled across the desert, and the gunslinger followed.</i> It immediately plunges you into a chase scene with an urge to know more and see what happens.<br /><br />I needed something light and whimsical after my previous book, so this childhood YA reread fit the bill perfectly -- it was also such a breath of fresh air to (re)read something that is so wholly, unmitigatedly 5 stars from me. <i>Mortal Engines</i> is futuristic post-apocalyptic steampunk, by way of effortless worldbuilding that drops little tantalising hints about the past rather than hitting you with a history textbook about what happened to this world; in fact, it took me a while before I even fully realised that this was set thousands of years into the future. Which is the best kind of subtle, show-don't-tell way of worldbuilding.<br /><br />I <i>love</i> the landscape of the Hungry City Chronicles (I'm definitely going to devour the rest of the series), and think it would pair well with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8198773.The_Half_Made_World__The_Half_Made_World___1_" title="The Half-Made World (The Half-Made World, #1) by Felix Gilman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Half-Made World</a> &amp; the computer game <a href="http://www.inklestudios.com/80days/" rel="nofollow noopener">80 Days</a> -- what with the former's dusty landscapes ground down under massive holy Engines, and the latter's retropunk technology and flying cities.<br /><br />It's fun. It's just plain <i>fun</i>, part- tongue-in-cheek whimsy with extravagantly named characters (e.g. Thaddeus Valentine is an awesome pulpy name) and living cities and airship adventures -- to the extent that I almost rated this as middle-grade, until some really tremendously dark shit kept happening, which lodged it firmly in the young adult camp. There's also gruesome, startling murder; slavery; real loss (there are so! many! upsetting! deaths!); plus some slight body horror in the form of the Stalkers; and some dystopian worldbuilding in what London has become. Some sequences are really truly terrifying!<br /><br />And yet it's also sweet, and tragic, and there's room for romance that isn't insta-love, and a nuanced anti-villain, and strong female characters, and even a total badass named Anna Fang: a half-Chinese, red-clad, dashing swash-buckling aviatrix spy (how much do I <a href="http://vignette2.wikia.nocookie.net/mortalengines/images/0/0d/Anna_fang_(1).jpg/revision/latest?cb=20141020180452" rel="nofollow noopener">love her</a>? let me <a href="http://66.media.tumblr.com/a321e2173ac26741848adb079ab41b62/tumblr_nj7rjgqTAN1qb8175o1_r2_500.png" rel="nofollow noopener">count the ways</a>). And Captain Khora, briefly as we see him, is an awesome captain from one of the African cities. LIKE I JUST. For being published in 2001, there's a bright touch of diversity in the novel. Themes of pseudo-capitalist consumption and environmental devastation and non-sustainability abound, too.<br /><br />Basically it's one of my favourite things, and I'm so glad that it held up. Highly recommended. Philip Reeve might wreck my gender reading ratio this year, damnit.<br /><br /><b>EDITED TO ADD:</b> Katelynn reminded me! This book is really incredibly cinematic -- Philip Reeve is/was an illustrator as well, which I think helps him craft strikingly vivid visuals in prose, much like Mike Carey did via his migration from comics -- and lo and behold, Peter Jackson is <a href="http://www.tracking-board.com/peter-jackson-to-write-mortal-engines-with-longtime-collaborator-christian-rivers-directing/" rel="nofollow noopener">adapting it</a>! I am so excited.<br /><br />Favourite quotes below, spoilery:<br /><blockquote>
  <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[He cut through the Twenty-First Century gallery, past the big plastic statues of Pluto and Mickey, animal-headed gods of lost America.<br /><br />***<br /><br />His tunic lay on the mud nearby, but he couldn’t find his shirt at all, until he crawled closer to the scarred girl and realized that she was busily tearing it into strips that she was using to bandage her wounded leg. “Hey!” he said. “That’s one of my best shirts!”<br /><br />“So?” she replied without looking up. “It’s one of my best legs.”<br /><br />***<br /><br />He smiled faintly, like somebody who had never seen a smile but had read a book on how to do it.<br /><br />***<br /><br />“Is it … dead?” asked Tom, his voice all quivery with fright.<br /><br />“A town just ran over him,” said Hester. “I shouldn’t think he’s very well….”<br /><br />***<br /><br />Was this what falling in love was like? Not something big and amazing that you knew about straight away, like in a story, but a slow thing that crept over you in waves until you woke up one day and found that you were head-over-heels with someone quite unexpected, like an Apprentice Engineer?<br /><br />***<br /><br />[A]lthough some were wounded, the only ones dead were a man called Weymouth, whom she had never spoken to, and Dr. Arkengarth. The old curator of ceramics lay near the door, looking indignant, as if death was a silly modern fad that he rather disapproved of.<br /><br />***<br /><br />The <i>Jenny Haniver</i> was filled with memories of Anna Fang: the mark of her mouth on a dirty mug, the print of her body on the unmade bunk, a half-read book on the flight deck, marked with a ribbon at page 205.<br /><br />***<br /><br />“You aren’t a hero, and I’m not beautiful, and we probably won’t live happily ever after,” she said. “But we’re alive, and together, and we’re going to be all right.” <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="12529355498693748543" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Gy935nPJ0TSuiGGpftGDA2aAYpJjEh7rbGbv+UXVmbfeONcrBGejGuskmOOEaWoIwr/wTPPFWTo9sdaxyVDNXg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }
